<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14628951365444099377">Sir Waldo Hawkridge was seldom refused anything, particularly not by unmarried young women who wanted his fortune and good name. He'd always been relentlessly pursued, and was ruthlessly determined to stay single. But then Sir Waldo came across not one, but two women who captured his interest--and found that one of them had the potential to capture his heart as well.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_881118959">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/881118959" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl" class="left imgcol" title="Tadiana ? Night Owl?"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1383845644p2/8734459.jpg" alt="Tadiana ? Night Owl?" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/881118959?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 23, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl" class="user" title="Tadiana ? Night Owl?">Tadiana ? Night Owl?</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32110.The_Nonesuch" title="Paperback 9780099474388" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=squeaky-clean-romance" class="actionLinkLite">squeaky-clean-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=not-another-misunderstanding" class="actionLinkLite">not-another-misunderstanding</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=you-call-that-an-ending" class="actionLinkLite">you-call-that-an-ending</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer881118959">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6677411431098292617">3 1/2 stars. I don't always care for Georgette Heyer's heroes and heroines, but this is a very likeable pair (even if their names make me wince): the witty, intelligent and kind Sir Waldo (also young and handsome, though you wouldn't guess it from his name) and the honorable, even-tempered and also intelligent Ancilla Trent, a lady in Reduced Circumstances who is now working as a governess. Ancilla is a capable, sensible person--my kind of heroine!--who knows how to manage a situation even when</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6677411431098292617">3 1/2 stars. I don't always care for Georgette Heyer's heroes and heroines, but this is a very likeable pair (even if their names make me wince): the witty, intelligent and kind Sir Waldo (also young and handsome, though you wouldn't guess it from his name) and the honorable, even-tempered and also intelligent Ancilla Trent, a lady in Reduced Circumstances who is now working as a governess. Ancilla is a capable, sensible person--my kind of heroine!--who knows how to manage a situation even when others around her are losing their heads. <br /><br />With such a rational pair, the craziness has to break out somewhere, and it does so in the form of Tiffany Wield, Miss Trent's charge, whose beauty drives the local young men to distraction and who is the most amazingly spoiled brat you'll ever have the dubious pleasure of meeting. Tiffany's behavior is <s>a little</s> over the top; she acts more like a 6 year old than a 17 year old, and I got thoroughly tired of reading about her antics. Luckily she doesn't fool either Waldo or Miss Trent. Minus one star for Too.Much.Tiffany.<br /><br />The other reason this isn't one of my favorite GH books: about 3/4 of the way through we get hit with that old Regency trope, the Big Misunderstanding. Happily, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Sir Waldo never loses hope and remains determined to get to the bottom of it, and  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>most of the time between the start of the misunderstanding and when it gets resolved is spent on other topics (Tiffany, of course), so the reader isn't put through the usual amount of agony. I give Heyer props for that. Still, it's a pretty far-fetched and, of course, unnecessary misunderstanding. The use of this trope--by far my least favorite plot device in this genre--made me knock part of another star off its rating. <br /><br />Favorite quote: "Mr Culver's carefully arranged locks were too lavishly pomaded to rise on end, but his eyes showed a tendency to start from their sockets." (Chapter 18)<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6677411431098292617">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_596363284">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/596363284" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/18780551-anne" class="left imgcol" title="Anne"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1437261844p2/18780551.jpg" alt="Anne" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/596363284?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 11, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/18780551-anne" class="user" title="Anne">Anne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32110.The_Nonesuch" title="Paperback 9780099474388" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=historical-romance" class="actionLinkLite">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=owned" class="actionLinkLite">owned</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=older-heroines" class="actionLinkLite">older-heroines</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=georgette-heyer" class="actionLinkLite">georgette-heyer</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=gentleman-like-heroes" class="actionLinkLite">gentleman-like-heroes</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=laugh-out-loud-funny" class="actionLinkLite">laugh-out-loud-funny</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=role-model-heroines" class="actionLinkLite">role-model-heroines</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=best-of-2013" class="actionLinkLite">best-of-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer596363284">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17297311675805134777"><strong> **Contains spoilers!!** <br /><br />4.5 stars<br /><br /><u>Things I loved:</u></strong><br /><br />1. Sir Waldo - I mean what's not to like?? He's handsome, rich, athletic, virtuous, idolized and a PHILANTHROPIST!! <em>Finally</em> a perfect hero who doesn't cringe at the mere mention of paupers! He wants his newly inherited estate, Broom Hall, to become a school for young orphan boys! Needless to say he won my deepest respect from the first (and managed to keep it!).<br /><br />2. Ancilla Trent. I LOVED HER!!! She was absolutely amazing! She was so genteel, elegan</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17297311675805134777"><strong> **Contains spoilers!!** <br /><br />4.5 stars<br /><br /><u>Things I loved:</u></strong><br /><br />1. Sir Waldo - I mean what's not to like?? He's handsome, rich, athletic, virtuous, idolized and a PHILANTHROPIST!! <em>Finally</em> a perfect hero who doesn't cringe at the mere mention of paupers! He wants his newly inherited estate, Broom Hall, to become a school for young orphan boys! Needless to say he won my deepest respect from the first (and managed to keep it!).<br /><br />2. Ancilla Trent. I LOVED HER!!! She was absolutely amazing! She was so genteel, elegant and sensible, and remained so throughout the story, even when she thought that she was being heedless because Sir Waldo had the disconcerting ability to throw her into flutters.<em>
  <strong> “ She decide that her wisest course would be to put him out of her mind. After reaching this conclusion she lay thinking about him until at last she fell asleep.”</strong>
</em> I felt extremely bad for her having to watch over that abominable wild-cat, known as Tiffany.<br /><br />3. Their first meeting. It was Beau.Ti.Ful.!!! Sparks flew all the way! You could feel the electricity in the air when they first looked upon each other! It was very well done.<br /><em>
  <strong> “Their eyes met, both pairs gray, hers very cool and clear, his faintly smiling”</strong>
</em><br /><br />4. Lord Lindeth ending up with Miss Chartley; they were both my favourite secondary characters and as soon as it was hinted at that they had the possibility of becoming a couple, I was all "Oh please, please Miss Heyer! Please have the presence of mind to make them end up together! To the devil with Tiffany!!". I was immensely scared that Tiffany would win Lindeth.<br /><br />5. Miss Chartley. She was awesome, from the few glimpses we had of her. I loved the episode in Leeds. Way to go Patience! She deserved a lot more attention than she got (from the characters and from Miss Heyer!) and should’ve been more into the spotlight than annoying, vexatious Tiffany. <br /><br />6. Sir Waldo and Miss Trent waltzing!!! <em>
  <strong>"With you or no one!"</strong>
</em> Gasp!!! SWOON!!!<br /><br />7. The simple plot! As much as I enjoy Heyer’s overpacked plots of cross-dressing/duels/gambling/drinking/elopements with wealthy handsome noblemen wearing wigs and mincing around on high heels, carrying fans, I really liked the calmer, country feel-good atmosphere of a good ol’ Regency comedy of manners taking place under the oh-so-hot sun of a Yorkshire summer.<br /><br />8. The Regency slang. Heyer went full out in this one! Most of the time it was pretty easy to use the context to determine the meaning of words/sentences, but I admit that there were a few instances when I didn’t particularly understand what was being said. But overall I really enjoyed it! Heyer sure knew how to write! Some of my favourite: <strong> “chuckfarthing fellow”, “Town Tulip”, “Top-of-the-Trees”, “nambypamby nonsense”, “ninny-hammer”</strong> and my new favourite expression <strong> “making a cake of oneself”</strong>!!!!<br /><br /><u>
  <strong> Things that annoyed me:</strong>
</u> <br /><br />1. Tiffany. She was just plainly atrociously IN.TO.LE.RA.BLE. As much as I appreciate villains and selfish, shallow characters, she was just too much!!And the fact that she was beautiful only made it worse! She didn’t deserve it! Which brings me to<br /><br />2. Every. Single. Man dangling around her!!! It was so irritating to hear of so-and-so going after Miss Wield and so-and-so being jealous, and then Sir Waldo (yes, <em>Sir Waldo</em>!!!!!!) giving her encouragement from time to time! Of course we know that he is by no means taking in with her, but still! I would have loved to hear instead that he was <em>the one man</em> who refrained from flirting with her, even if he wanted to “teach her a lesson”.<br /><br />3. Speaking of which, she never does learn her lesson!!! She gets what she wants in the end!!!! SHE GOES TO LONDON!!!! Well, I was only glad for the sake of everyone else, particularly the Staples folk, that they were to be rid of her!<br /><br />4. Miss Trent pretending that she isn’t in love with the Nonesuch when he proposes to her, because she thinks he has a bunch of illegitimate children!!! Of all the absurdities! And, what was very upsetting, the fact that she WON’T ASK HIM POINT-BLANK WHAT EXACLTY IT MEANS THAT HE HAD WRETCHED BRATS!!! Ah! I know that she was very picky with the proprieties, but come on! She could have found a way to ask him tactfully what was up! But no! Instead he had to be rejected, when it had been so obvious that he was as virtuous and straitlaced as she was, and so profoundly in love with her!! Poor Sir Waldo!!<br /><br />5. As much as I love the Regency and its customs and manners, I can’t help but being a trifle annoyed at the exaggeration as to what is sometimes considered an “impropriety”. No lady can do anything by herself, but God forbid she asks the help of any gentleman for she is sure then of being reproached of setting her cap at him, which would be even worse! That part when some of the old matrons are gossiping about how Miss Trent is trying to catch Sir Waldo was too much to bear! All because they danced (twice! Oh, my Lord! How improper!), and he lead her on his arm to supper, and then later in the evening wrapped a shawl around her. It wasn’t as though they were seen making out on the terrace! And besides, as it never occurred to them, that hum, hello, maybe the reason for Sir Waldo’s singling Miss Trent out might be that he is IN LOVE WITH HER?!?!? Why else would he flirt with the <em>governess</em>?!?<br /><br />6. The word lief. It was decidedly over-used. I don’t mind the abuse of “devil” or “devilish” or “damn” or “dash”, but if I come across “lief” again!! Argh!!!<br /><br />7. The fact that we are never given any insight into Sir Waldo’s developing passion for Miss Trent. We all <em>know</em> he’s falling for her, and as much as I appreciate Heyer’s “show don’t tell”, I would have liked a tad bit more of what was going on inside his head. We read about Miss Trent’s developing feelings, so why not his? I wanted to know from <em>his</em> perspective why he had fallen in love with Ancilla. We got what Laurie thought on the matter! Like, who cared about Laurie, right?!?<br /><br />8. The ending. If I can even call it that. I know Heyer loves to wrap things up pretty quickly, as though she thinks that after the hero and heroine have kissed it’s time to end the story as quickly as she can, lest she should be tempted to get them into bed- action (LOL I don’t think so! I’m kidding she wouldn’t!), but really?!? That was exaggerated! A <em>little bit more </em> interaction between the two lovers after they are agreed to get married! I am reviewing the book right now, but I still feel like I haven’t finished it!<br /><br />When all’s said and done, however, my annoyances weren’t so profound as to out-weigh my overall enjoyment of <em>The Nonesuch</em>. The book was a marvel. Whatever I’m going to read next might seem pretty poor after this!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17297311675805134777">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_122868574">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122868574" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2439366-natalie" class="left imgcol" title="Natalie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1284990646p2/2439366.jpg" alt="Natalie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/122868574?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 24, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2439366-natalie" class="user" title="Natalie">Natalie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32110.The_Nonesuch" title="Paperback 9780099474388" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer122868574">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7252030263196932383">I just love Georgette Heyer. This is a 5 star book of hers for completely different reasons then "Arabella", "Frederica" or "The Grand Sophie" (all favorite Heyer books), yet it's not quite the same as "These Old Shades" or "Devil's Cub" (My two other favorites). The first three (and several others of hers) always have me laughing out loud when I read. The last two, are romances that make my heart beat just a little faster along with wonderful adventures. The Nonesuch isn't quite the same as any</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7252030263196932383">I just love Georgette Heyer. This is a 5 star book of hers for completely different reasons then "Arabella", "Frederica" or "The Grand Sophie" (all favorite Heyer books), yet it's not quite the same as "These Old Shades" or "Devil's Cub" (My two other favorites). The first three (and several others of hers) always have me laughing out loud when I read. The last two, are romances that make my heart beat just a little faster along with wonderful adventures. The Nonesuch isn't quite the same as any of these. It has some very funny parts, but more every day life kind of funny then Saturday Night Live kind of funny. It's the two main characters that really sells this book for me. The "Nonesuch" himself is such a good man. He seems almost too good to be true, but really, it's a romance so why can't he be? Miss Trent is not so young as some of Heyer's heroines (she's one of the older types that Heyer occasionally writes so well). She's smart, and elegant, yet she has a sense of humor. Really what I like about this book is the romance that blooms so naturally. It makes total sense and it evolves very naturally. The obstacles all come from outside sources (with only very little misunderstanding between the two that is completely understandable). So often romances get caught up in the "they love each other and have to completely misunderstand each other to make it interesting" plot line. I get frustrated when the characters make their own troubles and just end up frustrating me. This book was satisfying romance that was also interesting through and through. I would recommend this to anyone who likes romance. Especially to those who are interested in trying Heyer again.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7252030263196932383">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1276277442">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1276277442" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/21073355-jade" class="left imgcol" title="jade"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1381337827p2/21073355.jpg" alt="jade" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1276277442?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 11, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/21073355-jade" class="user" title="jade">jade</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32110.The_Nonesuch" title="Paperback 9780099474388" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/21073355-jade?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1276277442">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9252648883860767193">Many people couldn't stand Tiffany. She's hands down the most nasty female character I've read in Heyer's universe. Maybe because I'd been prepared by people's irritation of her, I found Tiffany's absolute self-absorption and selfishness very entertaining. Every scene with her, whether it's throwing temper tantrum or merely opening her mouth, gave me a good laugh. Reading men of quality falling prey to her beauty until they were hit by her nasty temper and came out of the stupor was more fun tha</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9252648883860767193">Many people couldn't stand Tiffany. She's hands down the most nasty female character I've read in Heyer's universe. Maybe because I'd been prepared by people's irritation of her, I found Tiffany's absolute self-absorption and selfishness very entertaining. Every scene with her, whether it's throwing temper tantrum or merely opening her mouth, gave me a good laugh. Reading men of quality falling prey to her beauty until they were hit by her nasty temper and came out of the stupor was more fun than reading the subdued romance between Sir Waldo and Miss Trent, and it didn't help that the misunderstanding between them toward the end seemed a bit forced to me. What did irritate me a little was Miss Trent's ever present impulse to feel sorry and to patch things up for this heartless Tiffany. With her constant thinking "she's just a child", you'd think Tiffany was a 6-year-old instead of a young woman ready for the marriage market. <br /><br />That's why it's so satisfying in the end when Miss Trent tried but FAILED to stop Sir Waldo from giving Tiffany a long overdue stern set down. But this ending! Ugh!! It's better than Heyer's <em>Black Sheep</em>, but not by much. It kills me that I'll never know how Tiffany reacted to Sir Waldo's brilliant, crushing words. With Laurence cheering Sir Waldo on, that would've been such a delicious read!<br /><br />To me the story could've been tighter. More than once, I found myself skimming through lengthy thoughts of some minor characters. <br /><br />3.5 stars</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9252648883860767193">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer41911271">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5673624414316881523">3.5 stars. Very enjoyable, only the ending was a little abrupt. Heyer typically ends with the marriage proposal, and we actually get a few pages past that in this book, but I felt like some of the secondary characters were left hanging.<br /><br />This one is a relatively serious romance instead of pure comedy. The dialog is sparkling, as always, and the hero and heroine are likeble once you get past their names, the worst I've seen from Heyer yet: Waldo Hawkbridge and Ancilla Trent.</span>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=brit-lit" class="actionLinkLite">brit-lit</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer33004669">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4445839648395366217">Another Heyer I've re-read many times over the years. 'Tis a slightly older couple romance. I like the sensible heroine, and envy her endless patience, though am slightly irritated by how uptight and prudish she is. The character drawing of the annoying Beauty is so spot on, I cringe every time I read her. The hero is, naturally, perfect. Older men approve of him, younger men want to be him, ladies swoon over him. He's a bit over-perfect for me, but his witty put-downs are so hilarious I repeate</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4445839648395366217">Another Heyer I've re-read many times over the years. 'Tis a slightly older couple romance. I like the sensible heroine, and envy her endless patience, though am slightly irritated by how uptight and prudish she is. The character drawing of the annoying Beauty is so spot on, I cringe every time I read her. The hero is, naturally, perfect. Older men approve of him, younger men want to be him, ladies swoon over him. He's a bit over-perfect for me, but his witty put-downs are so hilarious I repeatedly forgive him for being a paragon of all virtues.</span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3727861-andrea?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3727861-andrea?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1324245360">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17990286180635081936">Another sensible heroine (and a marvellously insufferable younger charge). The mutual falling in love part happens quite early, and we need a big misunderstanding to delay the conclusion of the story.<br /><br />Tiffany (the charge) really is a revolting girl, but I was interested in the section, early on, where Tiffany points out that it's silly for her to pretend that she's not beautiful when she's perfectly able to see that she's beautiful, and everyone tells her it's so. This reminded me of the experime</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17990286180635081936">Another sensible heroine (and a marvellously insufferable younger charge). The mutual falling in love part happens quite early, and we need a big misunderstanding to delay the conclusion of the story.<br /><br />Tiffany (the charge) really is a revolting girl, but I was interested in the section, early on, where Tiffany points out that it's silly for her to pretend that she's not beautiful when she's perfectly able to see that she's beautiful, and everyone tells her it's so. This reminded me of the experiment some girls and women have tried by simply agreeing when some random guy on social media tells them they're beautiful/hot - and then instantly turns on her when she doesn't modestly protest that she's not. Even just saying "thanks" can garner a negative reaction.<br /><br />This is (to a somewhat lesser degree) true for men as well (a guy would be able to say 'thanks', I think, but would only sometimes be able to carry off a "yes" or "I know"). It's a virtue to be modest, apparently, but for a beautiful person to respond with a disclaimer in response to a compliment is a kind of mandatory social lie.<br /><br />We don't, after all, truly believe those beautiful people who say: "Oh, not really", or "You're being too generous" in response to a compliment (unless we think they've got an incredibly low self-esteem). The response is the equivalent of covering your mouth when you burp even though it doesn't hide that it happened, or stop any noise.<br /><br />Mandatory social lies. We really are an odd species.<br /><br />Reasonably good narrator.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17990286180635081936">...more</a>

          </span>

  <a href="/user/show/2329228-amy" class="left imgcol" title="Amy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1433629372p2/2329228.jpg" alt="Amy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/147825266?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 12, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2329228-amy" class="user" title="Amy">Amy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/3497114-the-nonesuch" title="Hardcover " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=georgette-heyer" class="actionLinkLite">georgette-heyer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer147825266">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17686417758263431937">The Nonesuch by Georgette Heyer was, in a word or two, rather disapointing. It looked like a fun plot, with more of a male main character, but I was wrong on both accounts. Not that the plot wasn't fun, but it lacked what I've come to expect from Heyer. The plot was rather symplistic (dare I say far-fetched?) without the usual hilarious irony I've come to expect. The characters also suffered somewhat, more on them in a moment.<br />Ancilla Trent, though once from a noble family, now lives as the compa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17686417758263431937">The Nonesuch by Georgette Heyer was, in a word or two, rather disapointing. It looked like a fun plot, with more of a male main character, but I was wrong on both accounts. Not that the plot wasn't fun, but it lacked what I've come to expect from Heyer. The plot was rather symplistic (dare I say far-fetched?) without the usual hilarious irony I've come to expect. The characters also suffered somewhat, more on them in a moment.<br />Ancilla Trent, though once from a noble family, now lives as the companion/governess in the home of a wealthy widow, caring for the woman's niece, Tiffany Weild. Tiffany is beautiful, spoiled, petted, wealthy, and completely untamable. Only Ms. Trent has been able to control the ambitious brat. <br />When Sir Waldo Hawkridge, dubbed "The Nonesuch" for his sporting abilities and the talk of London, inherits a run-down estate from a distant cousin, he decides to visit, there meeting the spoiled Beauty and her governess. <br />What follows is pretty much a love story between Ancilla and Sir Waldo. Sir Waldo's nephew, Lord Lindeth, shows up, falls in and out of love a few times, and pretty much just adds to the "romantic" plot in general. Another cousin of even less interest shows up, flirts around a bit, and attempts to be useful. Overall, I found them all disapointing. Ancilla is not really memorable, a bit like the main character from Persuasion. She's very virtuous (which I rather liked) yet young, clever...and rather boring. She falls in love with Sir Waldo, but it really isn't quite believable. <br />I guess the plot just lacked...something. All the romances tied up neatly, with supringly little issues. In fact, the climax was so easily overcome, I was quite suprised to find the book over. The ending was abrupt....<br />I'm just going to take a stagger and guess she wrote this early on. It holds hints of the wonderful work Heyer is capable of, but isn't her best. I'd much rather reccomend <a title="The Grand Sophy by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/261689.The_Grand_Sophy">The Grand Sophy</a> or <a title="Cotillion  by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311165.Cotillion_">Cotillion</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17686417758263431937">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer697409163">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer343508399232474116">Definitely <em>not</em> my favourite Heyer. It seemed to drag, even. Sir Waldo and Miss Trent are too good to be true; Lord Lindeth isn't far behind; Tiffany is just too bad to be true! Perhaps over-familiarity with Heyer is breeding contempt, but mostly I think it's just that I found the conflict so manufactured -- one of my least favourite tropes ever: the mistaken meaning, for example -- and I found the various combinations of characters pretty insipid. Tiffany could've brought more life to it if she</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText343508399232474116">Definitely <em>not</em> my favourite Heyer. It seemed to drag, even. Sir Waldo and Miss Trent are too good to be true; Lord Lindeth isn't far behind; Tiffany is just too bad to be true! Perhaps over-familiarity with Heyer is breeding contempt, but mostly I think it's just that I found the conflict so manufactured -- one of my least favourite tropes ever: the mistaken meaning, for example -- and I found the various combinations of characters pretty insipid. Tiffany could've brought more life to it if she were just a little easier to sympathise with, but she's like all the worst parts of the impulsive heroines of Sprig Muslin, Charity Girl and, indeed, the secondary heroine in Lady of Quality, without their good sides.<br /><br />In fact, listing all those makes me think regretfully of how similar Heyer novels can be to one another in some details. Perhaps it's time for a break. Alas. But then, this one didn't really make me laugh, or even raise a flutter, which is <em>not</em> a charge I can lay at the door of most of her novels.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="343508399232474116">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1355401967">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1355401967" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5858699-kavita" class="left imgcol" title="Kavita"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1315387023p2/5858699.jpg" alt="Kavita" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1355401967?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 08, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5858699-kavita" class="user" title="Kavita">Kavita</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32110.The_Nonesuch" title="Paperback 9780099474388" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5858699-kavita?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5858699-kavita?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1355401967">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14511744630754064463">I think the main romance was killed for me before it even started because of the name of the hero. Being an Archie comics fan, the name Waldo conjured up <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.mightycrusaders.net/a_images/waldo.9.jpg">images of this person</a> in my mind, and it was hard to get him out of my head. That said, I did like the main characters and some of the supporting characters too. However, unlike the usual Heyer novel, there were far too many characters and some of them blended into each other for me. I enjoyed the scenes of the spoilt Tiffany more than anyone e</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14511744630754064463">I think the main romance was killed for me before it even started because of the name of the hero. Being an Archie comics fan, the name Waldo conjured up <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.mightycrusaders.net/a_images/waldo.9.jpg">images of this person</a> in my mind, and it was hard to get him out of my head. That said, I did like the main characters and some of the supporting characters too. However, unlike the usual Heyer novel, there were far too many characters and some of them blended into each other for me. I enjoyed the scenes of the spoilt Tiffany more than anyone else, because she at least brought some vivacity and interest into the story, which was otherwise missing.<br /><br />The plot is not as tightly structured as it could have been. After many chapters of hanging out with each other as friends, we are suddenly shown that Ancilla had always loved Waldo from the moment she met him. It made no sense. There were too many angles started by the author and some of them didn't lead anywhere. The misunderstanding between the main couple was also rather forced and unrealistic. I rather liked the original idea of Ancilla thinking herself beneath Waldo and was upset by the local people's opinion, which could have been developed instead of going on a stupid tangent.<br /><br />I also wonder whether real Regency guardians wouldn't have given a girl like Tiffany a few hard slaps and taken away her privileges until she comes to her senses. The sympathetic and easygoing attitude shown towards Tiffany, who pretty much goes through the novel upsetting people, throwing tantrums and doing outrageous things, seems more a reflection of modern sensibilities than anything parents or guardians would have considered at any time in the past.<br /><br />Until the end, I considered this a 3-star book, but the abrupt ending was terrible. We are left without knowing what happens with Tiffany, how Laurence deals with his financial problems, how Mrs Underhill deals with the entire drama at the end - absolutely no idea. Just having the main couple's misunderstanding cleared doesn't lead to the end of the story! Tiffany is used as a plot device throughout the book and it is galling that she does not get a finale.<br /><br />Overall, the main problem is that this book is not fun, unlike what I have come to expect of Heyer. None of the witty dialogue, no comic situations, nothing. Without Tiffany, this novel would be just two mildly boring people falling in love. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14511744630754064463">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/387701810?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 27, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4579541-sally" class="user" title="Sally">Sally</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/10273851-the-nonesuch" title="Audible Audio " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4579541-sally?shelf=audiobooks" class="actionLinkLite">audiobooks</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer387701810">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12650215467709970840">Ahhhh, Georgette Heyer! I've read enough of her books to expect that each one will give me hours of pleasant reading (or listening) and there will always be at least a touch of romance, even in the mysteries. Although I wouldn't place The Nunesuch in my top favorites, I do see it as one with some uniqueness in characters and situations, a demonstration of Heyer's creativity with presenting possibilities, problems and resolutions.<br /><br />This one is a romance, and one in which the main romantic couple is</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12650215467709970840">Ahhhh, Georgette Heyer! I've read enough of her books to expect that each one will give me hours of pleasant reading (or listening) and there will always be at least a touch of romance, even in the mysteries. Although I wouldn't place The Nunesuch in my top favorites, I do see it as one with some uniqueness in characters and situations, a demonstration of Heyer's creativity with presenting possibilities, problems and resolutions.<br /><br />This one is a romance, and one in which the main romantic couple is beyond the age of the silliness of Regency debutants and young, foolish rich young men. Instead of centering on a man and woman who fall in love after seeming to hate each other and bandy with much sarcasm, as many of these types of stories do (including many of the Heyer romances) there is a spark of attraction from the beginning that triumphs through overcoming preconceived notions and a comedy-of-errors type of miscommunication. If for no other reason, I raced through this novel to reach the anticipated satisfactory resolution.<br /><br />So many times I have read stories where there is a character who behaves so badly, either from selfishness or evil motives, that I find I love to hate them. However, I think this is the first time I wanted to jump into the story myself, grab the spoiled, tantrum-throwing young woman by the shoulders and shake her until her teeth rattled and to give those characters who put up with the tantrums a good talking to. This must be a sign that the writing is so exceptional that the characters feel as if they are real.<br /><br />I would not recommend this one as a first Heyer read, but if you like Heyer, definitely include this in your to-read list.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12650215467709970840">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14684538493361704911">2 ½ stars. I was angry with the refusal to communicate. But the rest was enjoyable.<br /><br />STORY BRIEF:<br />Nonesuch is defined as a model of excellence or perfection. Sir Waldo is called the Nonesuch because of his sporting accomplishments and skill with horses. He is wealthy. He establishes and supports orphanages that care for, educate, and provide children with skills. He recently inherited Broom Hall, a rundown estate near the town of Oversett. Waldo stays there to oversee repairs and improvements. He plans to turn it into an orphanage. His cousin Julian accompanies him. While there, Waldo and Julian meet and interact with a number of people who live in Oversett.<br /><br />Ancilla had a season but didn’t fall in love. Her family is low on money so she gets a job as a teacher in a girls’ school. Tiffany attended this school and was so bad she got kicked out. Tiffany was sent to live with her aunt Mrs. Underhill in Oversett. Since Ancilla was the only person Tiffany would listen to, Mrs. Underhill hires Ancilla to be Tiffany’s governess/companion. Tiffany’s parents died leaving her wealthy. She is vain, selfish, narcissistic, irritating, obnoxious, spoiled, and extremely beautiful. She throws tantrums when she doesn’t get her way. She expects all men to fall in love with her.<br /><br />REVIEWER’S OPINION:<br />Like other Heyer books I love the various personalities, their interactions, and their conversations. I enjoyed watching Ancilla influence Tiffany. For example, Tiffany was upset that she wasn’t invited to someone’s party. Ancilla told her that the party would be held in a green room that would clash with Tiffany’s blue dress and why it would be better to … Tiffany accepted this. Tiffany’s behavior throughout the book was bad which was fun reading.<br /><br />Julian is blinded by Tiffany’s beauty. Waldo sees through Tiffany immediately. Tiffany is confused by Waldo’s hot vs. cold treatment of her.<br /><br />Waldo falls in love with Ancilla, but she won’t have him. The author used my pet peeve of a “big misunderstanding based on miscommunication.” When Waldo asked her what was wrong. I was angry that she would not tell him. This continued for much too long. For this reason I gave it 2 stars. If you don’t mind the big misunderstanding and her refusal to answer questions, but you’re a Heyer fan, then you should like it.<br /><br />As far as romance goes, this is typical Heyer with a friendship developing through the book, and a declaration of love at the very last moment. I would have liked more story between the couple after they declared their feelings. I also wanted to know what Waldo was going to do for Laurence at the end. Laurence wanted to borrow money for a business.<br /><br />The book description is somewhat misleading. It mentions “An impetuous flight” and “A Gallant rescue.” This happens at the very end of the book. Most of the story is about other things happening before that.<br /><br />I love the narrator Eve Matheson. I’d almost recommend this just to spend time with her. She has a lovely British accent and does all the voices well.<br /><br />DATA:<br />Unabridged audiobook length: 10 hours 49 minutes. Narrator: Eve Matheson. Swearing language: mild. Sexual content: none. Setting: 1816-1817 England. Book Published: 1962. Genre: regency romance.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14684538493361704911">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12169165867905097933">This Heyer stands out for making the well-rounded, virtuous characters so wonderfully attractive while the spoilt, self-interested fools couldn't be more tedious.<br /><br />The unassuming but well born Miss Ancilla Trent is governess to the spoilt and dangerously beautiful heiress Miss Tiffany Wield, and has a difficult time keeping her charge out of mischief.<br /><br />When the famed sportsman Sir Waldo Hawkridge inherits a dilapidated house in their village, Tiffany sets about adding him (as well as his cousins) to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12169165867905097933">This Heyer stands out for making the well-rounded, virtuous characters so wonderfully attractive while the spoilt, self-interested fools couldn't be more tedious.<br /><br />The unassuming but well born Miss Ancilla Trent is governess to the spoilt and dangerously beautiful heiress Miss Tiffany Wield, and has a difficult time keeping her charge out of mischief.<br /><br />When the famed sportsman Sir Waldo Hawkridge inherits a dilapidated house in their village, Tiffany sets about adding him (as well as his cousins) to her list of admirers. But Sir Waldo is perceptive, and it's not long before he's able to see past Miss Wield's dazzling beauty to notice her far more interesting governess.<br /><br />Highly recommended as an engaging romance with some substance. Reviewed for <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.GoodReadingGuide.com" target="_blank">www.GoodReadingGuide.com</a></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_967588759">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/967588759" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8076934-fiona-marsden" class="left imgcol" title="Fiona Marsden"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1400318079p2/8076934.jpg" alt="Fiona Marsden" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/967588759?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 14, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8076934-fiona-marsden" class="user" title="Fiona Marsden">Fiona Marsden</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32110.The_Nonesuch" title="Paperback 9780099474388" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer967588759">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15722132455530431030">I'm enjoying rediscovering Heyer in audiobook. The dialogue lends itself to this medium and with a good narrator can keep you smiling.<br /><br />Some people complain that Waldo is almost too good. I like that in a hero. Especially when he can be a manly man at the same time. Cos Waldo is very much a man. He is 'top-of-the-trees' in most forms of sport he undertakes so he will be *cough* well built and physically fit with lots of stamina.<br /><br />Ancilla is rather adorable, having put aside her hopes and dreams of l</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15722132455530431030">I'm enjoying rediscovering Heyer in audiobook. The dialogue lends itself to this medium and with a good narrator can keep you smiling.<br /><br />Some people complain that Waldo is almost too good. I like that in a hero. Especially when he can be a manly man at the same time. Cos Waldo is very much a man. He is 'top-of-the-trees' in most forms of sport he undertakes so he will be *cough* well built and physically fit with lots of stamina.<br /><br />Ancilla is rather adorable, having put aside her hopes and dreams of love and marriage to be an independent woman and not be a burden on her family. She deserves the best of happy endings. I love how Waldo brings out the mischievous side of her and her sense of humour which no-one else has ever really appreciated.<br /><br />Some have criticise her reaction to the misinformation about Waldo's secret. I think her reaction and reluctant belief is very credible. Heyer makes sure we understand that Ancilla's only real experience with the Corinthian Set of which Waldo is a leader, is though her cousin Bernard and his friends. These are very likely the kind of loose young men who would do what Ancilla believes Waldo to have done and not see it as very wrong. Combine this with the kindly meant warnings of Mrs Chartley, the half understood ramblings of Waldo's nephew, and it's not surprising that Ancilla is forced to believe the worst.<br /><br />The romance itself is very sweet, growing day by day to it's natural conclusion rather than a thunder-clap of Love at first sight. We can see how perfectly matched they are which makes it doubly hard when things go wrong.<br /><br />Ancilla's charge, Tiffany, is annoying and irritating but not enough to spoil the book, especially as we are meant to find her so. The other characters are well drawn and enjoyable. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15722132455530431030">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

              <a href="/review/list/949924-maria?shelf=historical-romance" class="actionLinkLite">historical-romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1306816607">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3945485108401691120">What a tangle of relationships! It was fun keeping up with who was interested in whom. Sir Waldo was a lot of fun, with his witty remarks and faked attention to Miss Wield. I tried to figure out why the young men were so fascinated by him, and finally realized that if he was the Michael Jordan of his day, that would explain a lot. The description of the characters from different levels of society was masterfully done, from near-cits to gentry to lower nobles. Miss Trent is a governess/companion</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3945485108401691120">What a tangle of relationships! It was fun keeping up with who was interested in whom. Sir Waldo was a lot of fun, with his witty remarks and faked attention to Miss Wield. I tried to figure out why the young men were so fascinated by him, and finally realized that if he was the Michael Jordan of his day, that would explain a lot. The description of the characters from different levels of society was masterfully done, from near-cits to gentry to lower nobles. Miss Trent is a governess/companion and steers a rocky course between being an employee and being treated as one of the family. Although she knows her own worth, she has chosen to work and feels she has left marriage possibilities behind, so when Sir Waldo walks into her life, she does not know quite what to do with him. He, on the other hand, knows exactly what he wants to do with her. Lovely Regency story.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3945485108401691120">...more</a>

              <a href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=regency-romance" class="actionLinkLite">regency-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=clean-romance" class="actionLinkLite">clean-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=kisses-only" class="actionLinkLite">kisses-only</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer667064352">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8991844991611899159">Sir Waldo Hawkridge has just learned that his late, unlamented cousin has just left him an estate and a fortune, to increase his already large fortune. Waldo's aunt covets the fortune for her son Julian (who doesn't need it or want it) and his cousin Lawrence covets the fortune for his own selfish reasons. Cousin George just makes wry comments about Waldo's plans for the estate. He intends to build an orphanage! How shocking! Sir Waldo ignores everyone's comments and takes Julian with him north</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8991844991611899159">Sir Waldo Hawkridge has just learned that his late, unlamented cousin has just left him an estate and a fortune, to increase his already large fortune. Waldo's aunt covets the fortune for her son Julian (who doesn't need it or want it) and his cousin Lawrence covets the fortune for his own selfish reasons. Cousin George just makes wry comments about Waldo's plans for the estate. He intends to build an orphanage! How shocking! Sir Waldo ignores everyone's comments and takes Julian with him north to Yorkshire to inspect Broom Hall. Intending to stay only a little while in a place where they know no one and no one knows them, they arrive to discover that Sir Waldo is something of a legend for being a noted Corinthian. All the local lads want to ape him. One local, however, strongly disapproves. Miss Ancilla Trent, governess/companion to Mrs. Underhill's daughter Charlotte and niece Tiffany Wield, is a well born woman of three-and-twenty who knows a thing or two about Corinthians - her cousin is one and she has no use for him and his idle set. Sir Waldo is shocked by her misconceptions and intrigued by the one lady who wants nothing to do with him. He sets out to correct that opinion! Meanwhile, his cousin Julian is bowled over by the beautiful Tiffany. Ancilla worries about what will happen when Julian discovers Tiffany may have the face of an angel but the disposition of a devil. Waldo worries what will happen if his aunt finds out his cousin is dangling after a merchant's heiress! Tiffany has her sights set on a higher prize but must make all the gentlemen adore her. Waldo has the perfect solution to Tiffany's scheme. Ancilla and Waldo find unexpected allies in each other as they go about chaperoning the young adults in the neighborhood. The young ladies and gentlemen find unexpected friendships and romance blossoms in this classic Georgette Heyer tale.<br /><br />I only gave this one 4 stars because there are several problems that keep it from being a 5 star book. First, there's an excessive amount of cant. I love how Heyer works in the period language but this is too much. When the men talk to each other it's almost unintelligible. She does a much better job in other books. Next, the romance is secondary to Tiffany, as Tiffany would wish it to be. Tiffany is a horrid, spoiled brat who needs to be taken firmly in hand. Someone should have spanked her when she was a toddler. She dominates the whole book with her tantrums and gets the last word in the novel. I love the central romance and how Ancilla and Waldo fall in love. This is one of the most romantic of Heyer's novels. There's speaking glances, exchanged looks, shared jokes and two waltzes. There was great potential here but the last third of the plot fell off. Then there's the misunderstanding. On my first read years ago, I couldn't figure out why Ancilla believed what she did. I can see it better now. She was scared of her own feelings and scared of what she thought she knew about Corinthians in general and Sir Waldo. She let the neighborhood gossips get to her. I think she let them bother her on purpose because she was afraid of having her heart broken and afraid of going to London among Waldo's friends where she wouldn't fit in. I don't know how she figured out the truth. It seems like a quick jump. The conclusion to the romance is incredibly unsatisfactory!<br /><br />The characters in this novel are fabulous as always. Tiffany is so incredibly horrid that readers just want to slap her. I empathized with her feelings in a few places but the way she acted was incredibly selfish and immature. She's young but she's old enough to know better. Ancilla is a great heroine when she's on page. She's not in the story a whole lot. She needed to be in it more. She's intelligent and strong, like most of Heyer's heroines. She has a sense of humor too and needs it to deal wit Tiffany. Sir Waldo is a dreamy hero. On my first reading, I fell in love with him right away. He's so witty and charming that I couldn't help myself. I love his sense of humor and the way he deals with Tiffany and his cousins. He's thoughtful and a philanthropist to boot. Not to mention his prowess at driving to an inch. <br /><br />This still remains in my top 10 Heyer list despite the problems. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8991844991611899159">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_27080576">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27080576" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/970517-katharine" class="left imgcol" title="Katharine"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1204774103p2/970517.jpg" alt="Katharine" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/27080576?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 12, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/970517-katharine" class="user" title="Katharine">Katharine</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32110.The_Nonesuch" title="Paperback 9780099474388" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/970517-katharine?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/970517-katharine?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer27080576">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2510738391612265282">This is another really good, satisfying Heyer. The dialogue is just as witty as <a title=" Cotillion" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Cotillion"> Cotillion</a> and the characters as likeable. I love Mrs. Underhill – she's like a squeezable Mrs. Bennet. I wish I knew her. The title character is admirable, not a rake, and there is no reforming involved. The secondary romance is very cute as well, and the north country setting is enjoyable although of course I have no idea how accurate it is.<br /><br />However, I do have to rate this lower than <em>Cotillion</em> for one reason: the he</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2510738391612265282">This is another really good, satisfying Heyer. The dialogue is just as witty as <a title=" Cotillion" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Cotillion"> Cotillion</a> and the characters as likeable. I love Mrs. Underhill – she's like a squeezable Mrs. Bennet. I wish I knew her. The title character is admirable, not a rake, and there is no reforming involved. The secondary romance is very cute as well, and the north country setting is enjoyable although of course I have no idea how accurate it is.<br /><br />However, I do have to rate this lower than <em>Cotillion</em> for one reason: the heroine, while not unlikeable, is not very memorable or lifelike. <br /><br />I've started to notice a pattern with Heyer. She is really good at characterization when her people are witty, impulsive, funny, charming, vulgar, ignorant, naive, or even rude. But every time she tries to portray someone reserved, quiet, cool, or shy, she fails. She tells us multiple times that Ancilla Trent is cool and elegant, but her actions and dialogue don't show it. Ancilla talks and thinks just like your average "older" Heyer heroine, with a lot of exclamation points. And nothing gives her a realistic character or sets her apart in any way. <br /><br />I think this is why I felt somewhat "meh" about <a title=" The Quiet Gentleman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20The%20Quiet%20Gentleman"> The Quiet Gentleman</a> – I believe I even commented in my review that the supposed gentleness of the hero was more talked about than felt. It's also why I adored <em>Cotillion</em>. None of the characters in that story were supposed to be shy, and as a result they were all vivid and memorable and really funny and charming. <br /><br />So... discussion point: was Heyer an extravert? </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2510738391612265282">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_223466639">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/223466639" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3596262-kelli" class="left imgcol" title="Kelli"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1424116898p2/3596262.jpg" alt="Kelli" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/223466639?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 06, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3596262-kelli" class="user" title="Kelli">Kelli</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32110.The_Nonesuch" title="Paperback 9780099474388" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3596262-kelli?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer223466639">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8149808069076764089">I think Ancilla + Waldo were the chosen character names because Georgette ran out of other ideas. Maybe because this one was published nearing the end of her career. Regardless, they are crazy names, which Heyer is known for--except this time, I tend to think someone in a book named Ancilla or Waldo, would be the evil characters. And they aren't. <br /><br />Both characters are actually some of Heyer's nicest. I get the feeling while reading, that Heyer was largely channeling Jane Eyre and a bit of Persuasi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8149808069076764089">I think Ancilla + Waldo were the chosen character names because Georgette ran out of other ideas. Maybe because this one was published nearing the end of her career. Regardless, they are crazy names, which Heyer is known for--except this time, I tend to think someone in a book named Ancilla or Waldo, would be the evil characters. And they aren't. <br /><br />Both characters are actually some of Heyer's nicest. I get the feeling while reading, that Heyer was largely channeling Jane Eyre and a bit of Persuasion.<br />This one has some good dialog, but only when certain people are present in the novel.<br />Sadly, halfway in, the pacing really slows down and I really didn't love it.<br /><br />This is a later Heyer, and she wrote a lot of older heroine taking care of younger girl stories when she got older. While that formula can work sometimes, the ones Heyer writes don't sparkle half as much as her other younger Heroine stories, aside from The Grand Sophy. <br />The ending bit picks up speed and is fun to read. This makes the book half enjoyable. Its the middle of the book that seems so long. The misunderstanding is, at first, annoying. But then Heyer turns it around and it's hilarious. The ending pretty much has all the shining moments. Tiffany is horridly difficult to read. She needs a huge smack. Her scenes make you annoyed and want to rush thru the novel, but Waldo has the best scenes, despite his silly name.<br />Definitely not the best Heyer, maybe this one would be for the ones wanting to read all her books and judge for themselves. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_49916210">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49916210" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2030200-bj-rose" class="left imgcol" title="BJ Rose"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1237763983p2/2030200.jpg" alt="BJ Rose" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/49916210?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 18, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2030200-bj-rose" class="user" title="BJ Rose">BJ Rose</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32110.The_Nonesuch" title="Paperback 9780099474388" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2030200-bj-rose?shelf=a-regency" class="actionLinkLite">a-regency</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2030200-bj-rose?shelf=keepers" class="actionLinkLite">keepers</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2030200-bj-rose?shelf=challenge-winter" class="actionLinkLite">challenge-winter</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer49916210">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9650719088206121057">Ancilla Trent was born into a respected but not affluent family, and moved in the first circles of society in Hertfordshire, until her father’s unlucky investments and untimely death left the family in financially uncomfortable circumstances. Her best hope was to marry well, but Ancilla would not marry where she did not love – but neither did she wish to be a burden on her brother or her uncle, so she became a schoolmistress and then a governess, thus putting her outside the accepted boundaries</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9650719088206121057">Ancilla Trent was born into a respected but not affluent family, and moved in the first circles of society in Hertfordshire, until her father’s unlucky investments and untimely death left the family in financially uncomfortable circumstances. Her best hope was to marry well, but Ancilla would not marry where she did not love – but neither did she wish to be a burden on her brother or her uncle, so she became a schoolmistress and then a governess, thus putting her outside the accepted boundaries of the socially acceptable. This is important in understanding her mind-set when The Nonesuch, Sir Waldo Hawkridge, comes to Oversett and begins paying attention to her. She does like his attention and his company, but she is convinced that he’s merely flirting with her and refuses to take his attention seriously. Just when she thinks his intentions are honorable, she learns that he is renovating Broom Hall for ‘his wretched brats’, and it’s obvious to her what <em>that</em> means! Surely a virtuous woman can have nothing to do with a man who has such a cavalier attitude about his libertine behavior! But he doesn’t act like a libertine, and his eyes twinkle so, and he has a wonderful sense of humor that keeps her on the edge of laughter, and his young cousin Julian certainly thinks highly of him – so what to do?!<br /><br />I loved the balance of youthful and mature romantic pairs, both of them strongly impacted by the selfish and self-centered Tiffany. Mrs. Chartley’s reading of Tiffany’s character was spot on: “…an odiously precocious little baggage who was wild to a fault, as vain as she was beautiful, and wholly wanting in character and disposition.” And Tiffany so often proved her right: she becomes livid with anger and has a raging tantrum on the street when she is ignored by <em>everyone</em> all because they’re caring for some <em>insignificant</em> little street boy who is seriously injured. Yup, that’s Tiffany, so, of course, this reader just kept waiting for her to get her comeuppance!<br /><br />A strong 4*<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9650719088206121057">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer17774664705035793666">*sigh*<br /><br />It's time to face the facts...<br />I still have a week or so before I have to return this book to the library but after struggling through 30% of its content defeat was staring me in the face.<br />Not only did I have problems figuring out who was who from the get-go, the prose in this book went over my head also. <br />It's one thing to tap on a screen for a word translation and a different thing entirely to attempt to read a paperback with the dictionary as a close companion.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText17774664705035793666">*sigh*<br /><br />It's time to face the facts...<br />I still have a week or so before I have to return this book to the library but after struggling through 30% of its content defeat was staring me in the face.<br />Not only did I have problems figuring out who was who from the get-go, the prose in this book went over my head also. <br />It's one thing to tap on a screen for a word translation and a different thing entirely to attempt to read a paperback with the dictionary as a close companion. The latter is too much work for me; it reminds me of reading for school whereas I'd prefer to read just for -ehm- ... entertainment.<br />There, I said it! <br />E.n.t.e.r.t.a.i.n.m.e.n.t.<br />Georgette Heyer, out of her grave, managed to rub my limitations of the English language right in my face.<br />Not having a PhD in English never felt so cruel...<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2083532204641517659">Sir Waldo is fabulously rich, and when he inherits yet another estate his relatives groan--out of envy, and also because they suspect Waldo will just turn the mansion into an orphanage. Their suspicions are correct. While getting the estate ready for his brats' arrival, Waldo notices Miss Trent, the poised governess to a local beauty. He tries to court Miss Trent (whose wry humor matches his own) while distangling his younger cousin from an infatuation with the spoiled beauty.<br /><br />Funny and sweet. Th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2083532204641517659">Sir Waldo is fabulously rich, and when he inherits yet another estate his relatives groan--out of envy, and also because they suspect Waldo will just turn the mansion into an orphanage. Their suspicions are correct. While getting the estate ready for his brats' arrival, Waldo notices Miss Trent, the poised governess to a local beauty. He tries to court Miss Trent (whose wry humor matches his own) while distangling his younger cousin from an infatuation with the spoiled beauty.<br /><br />Funny and sweet. The cant terms Heyer uses so liberally are a little less obtrusive here, and her hero and heroine are wonderful fun to read about. I do with it ended a bit less abruptly.</span>
