<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1482573115">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1482573115" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7217945-christopher" class="left imgcol" title="Christopher"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Christopher" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1482573115?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7217945-christopher" class="user" title="Christopher">Christopher</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32110.The_Nonesuch" title="Paperback 9780099474388" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1482573115">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10357101731376632344">Definitely not my kind of book, as it annoyed me far more often than not. The hero’s character was excessively annoying. The reader is told <em>constantly</em> that he is an absolute paragon, but the little of his character that is shown didn't seem to match this description. To me he came across jaded, bored, only exerts himself as far as it amuses him or in response to guilt, and generally didn't seem any different than a typical rakish hero. He’s more polite, I guess. The best thing about him is that</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10357101731376632344">Definitely not my kind of book, as it annoyed me far more often than not. The hero’s character was excessively annoying. The reader is told <em>constantly</em> that he is an absolute paragon, but the little of his character that is shown didn't seem to match this description. To me he came across jaded, bored, only exerts himself as far as it amuses him or in response to guilt, and generally didn't seem any different than a typical rakish hero. He’s more polite, I guess. The best thing about him is that he does show a consistency in his regard for the heroine. I really liked the heroine and her practical mind, but it annoyed me to no end that she too threw her good sense out the window whenever the hero was near. My favorite part was when she resolves not to be taken in and leads him on a merry chase. I wasn’t overly annoyed by Tiffany, but I was very annoyed by the fact that the hero and heroine constantly scrape and bow to please her, even if they do it as a form of manipulation. The whole book felt like a badly written romance. There’s no humor to speak of, no adventure, no grand farce that everything builds up to, nothing of the key elements that I have enjoyed in Heyer’s other novels. The plot is driven by some rather insipid romantic conflicts and misunderstandings, especially at the end. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ The whole misunderstanding with the “wretched brats” was ridiculous on multiple levels. Correct me if I’m wrong, but I reread that section a few times and it seemed to me that the heroine’s line of reasoning is that: the hero has illegitimate children -&gt; therefore, he has had affairs with other women -&gt; therefore, he is a libertine and will not be faithful during their marriage. On one hand, the reality that he has no children does not exclude him from having had affairs. On the contrary, his considerable experience with the fairer sex is heavily implied. On the other hand, even if he had fathered children that doesn’t mean he wouldn’t be faithful. I could certainly see why the heroine wouldn’t want to deal with his illegitimate offspring, but it seems to speak in favor of his character if he wanted to take care of them. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I don’t know, it all just seemed so absurd.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10357101731376632344">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1263701319">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1263701319" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6945307-damaskcat" class="left imgcol" title="Damaskcat"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1395844674p2/6945307.jpg" alt="Damaskcat" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1263701319?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 28, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6945307-damaskcat" class="user" title="Damaskcat">Damaskcat</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/12874725-the-nonesuch" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1263701319">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6712722856556303387">This is one the most light hearted of Georgette Heyer's Regency novels and one of my favourites. Sir Waldo Hawkridge inherits Broom Hall in Yorkshire. He visits the house with his cousin Julian Lindeth and both of them quickly become popular in the neighbourhood most especially with Miss Tiffany Weild and the other young ladies in the area. But Sir Waldo seems to be more interested in Tiffany's companion Miss Ancilla Trent.<br /><br />I loved the characters in this novel - Ancilla and Sir Waldo especially.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6712722856556303387">This is one the most light hearted of Georgette Heyer's Regency novels and one of my favourites. Sir Waldo Hawkridge inherits Broom Hall in Yorkshire. He visits the house with his cousin Julian Lindeth and both of them quickly become popular in the neighbourhood most especially with Miss Tiffany Weild and the other young ladies in the area. But Sir Waldo seems to be more interested in Tiffany's companion Miss Ancilla Trent.<br /><br />I loved the characters in this novel - Ancilla and Sir Waldo especially. Mrs Underhill, Tiffany's aunt, is also excellent with her down to earth practicality and common sense. Tiffany herself is a monster of selfishness and probably one of Heyer's most unpleasant female creations but she is so unaware of her behaviour that people soon realise what she's like even though they are impressed by her looks when they first meet her.<br /><br />The dialogue and the plot are as ever extremely well done and no one can match Heyer for her portrayal of the Regency period with its different manners and morals. <br /><br />I have also recently listened to the audio book version and can report that it works seamlessly with the Kindle edition and you can easily go from listening to one to reading the other.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6712722856556303387">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_62995682">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62995682" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/162084-sherwood-smith" class="left imgcol" title="Sherwood Smith"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1409524068p2/162084.jpg" alt="Sherwood Smith" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/62995682?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 10, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/162084-sherwood-smith" class="user" title="Sherwood Smith">Sherwood Smith</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2122852.The_Nonesuch" title=" 9780330244213" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/162084-sherwood-smith?shelf=siver-fork" class="actionLinkLite">siver-fork</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer62995682">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8869897114700537993">There are a lot of things going for this one--two heroes who play off one another well, and a governess heroine who is one of Heyer's best. Add in some nifty side characters, and it almost is a good one, except for Tiffany Wield, one of Heyer's unpleasant characters. <br /><br />Tiffany isn't going to change, so long, LONG scenes with her being a bitch wear thin real fast. I'd call this one 3.5 because of that aspect, but of course mileage always varies.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QYwV5rp2Vt6u6HgyAA1KVC3JgZB9BbWC82A+UHlieAQkWCo1SKRCJCIwDIl+bKzmZD5CiTTY8iiZaTvCtfeOQQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('khpROWmBbTonQK7kTUNpPXst77Cpd/DcFay4aqlE3FH3zm7qm1N5wKuY2l8zIo+PMtosqeCqt3Z/pb34ZdEqFA==')})

Her father, however, has far grander designs for Miss Fortune.…Caro is to become the companion of Mrs. Catling, the rich, fierce widow of her father\'s old colonel. As Mrs. Catling amuses herself by tormenting her relatives and servants, Caro resolves to make the best of the situation, and soon her beauty and intelligence attract the attentions of male admirers. Surrounded by people with an alarming readiness to reveal each other\'s confidences, Caroline is exasperated to find herself implicated in their indiscretions. But will Miss Fortune be able to avoid losing her reputation without losing her head? To prove he is not an idle fop only concerned with sartorial pleasures, Alistair agrees to help his old friend, Lord Gordmor, by traveling to the wilds of Derbyshire to convince Gordmor\'s neighbors to support the nobleman\'s proposal to build a canal. Upon arriving, Alistair, a famous war hero and eligible bachelor, finds everyone couldn\'t be nicer, everyone except for respectable, practical, spinsterish Mirabel Oldridge. The last thing Mirabel wants is for her tranquil little corner of England to be destroyed by a noisy, nasty canal, and she is prepared to use every weapon at her disposal--including her disheveled coiffure and unstylish wardrobe--to stop Alistair. RITA Award-winning Chase presents a splendidly written tale of two people trying desperately not to fall in love. Chase\'s beguiling blend of deliciously complex characters, potent sexual chemistry, and sparkling wit give this superb romance a richness and depth readers will treasure.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer">About Georgette Heyer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer"><img alt="18067" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1336748892p2/18067.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer10624403762151923991">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a title=" The Black Moth" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth"> The Black Moth</a>.<br /><br />In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer, and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance novel and one thriller each year.<br /><br />Hey</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10624403762151923991">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a title=" The Black Moth" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth"> The Black Moth</a>.<br /><br />In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer, and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance novel and one thriller each year.<br /><br />Heyer was an intensely private person who remained a best selling author all her life without the aid of publicity. She made no appearances, never gave an interview and only answered fan letters herself if they made an interesting historical point. She sometimes wrote under the pseudonym Stella Martin.<br /><br />Her Regencies were inspired by <a title=" Jane Austen" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1265._Jane_Austen"> Jane Austen</a>, but unlike Austen, who wrote about and for the times in which she lived, Heyer was forced to include copious information about the period so that her readers would understand the setting. While some critics thought her novels were too detailed, others considered the level of detail to be Heyer's greatest asset.<br /><br />Heyer remains a popular and much-loved author, known for essentially establishing the historical romance genre and its subgenre Regency romance.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10624403762151923991">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Georgette Heyer...</a>
